            <p class="base-aside-card__subtitle font-sans text-sm text-color-text leading-regular break-words overflow-anywhere
                line-clamp-2">
              
          📊AI models are now hitting genius-level IQ scores

In a series of tests using the official Mensa Norway IQ quiz, multiple AI models scored between 130 and 148 IQ, the same range as the top 2% of humans.

Yes, you read that right:
Some models are now outperforming humans on abstract reasoning, pattern recognition, and problem-solving.

The new AI intelligence curve:
➡️130–148 IQ → Top performers
Models from OpenAI, Google, and Anthropic landed here
➡️100–125 IQ → The majority
Solid reasoning, above-average, human-like performance
➡️Below 90 IQ → A few underwhelming vision models
Struggled with multi-modal reasoning tasks

These scores were averaged over seven rounds of testing. Not a one-off.

Why it matters:
This isn’t about predicting the next word in a sentence.
This is about whether a model can think.

These tests measure the kind of intelligence used in:
✔️ Strategic decisions
✔️ Complex research
✔️ High-stakes problem solving

And for the first time, a few models are showing they can reason at levels most people can’t.

➡️The real takeaway:
The AI bell curve now looks like the human one, except some models are starting to stretch into territory we used to call genius.

That changes the game.

Get curated GenAI updates that actually matter to you. 
Choose your interests: https://hubs.li/Q03D3f080 

#artificialintelligence #generativeai #gpt5 #futureofwork #llm #machinelearning

            <p class="base-aside-card__subtitle font-sans text-sm text-color-text leading-regular break-words overflow-anywhere
                line-clamp-2">
              
          Jabbr raises 32 million kroner to bring AI to combat sports

The Danish company Jabbr has raised 32 million kroner in new funding to develop its AI-powered platform for analyzing combat sports. The investment round is led by the Silicon Valley fund Buckley Ventures with participation from PSV Tech, Olympic gold medalist André Ward, and the venture firm Seven Seven Six 7️⃣7️⃣6️⃣ founded by Reddit, Inc. creator Alexis Ohanian Sr.

Jabbr’s technology uses cameras and artificial intelligence to analyze and score fights in real time. The goal is to make judging more objective and to give athletes, trainers, and broadcasters detailed insights into performance. The first production batch of 300 systems is already fully pre-ordered and expected to be delivered next year.

Founded in Copenhagen by Allan Svejstrup Nielsen and Elias Obeid, Jabbr has already attracted global attention after delivering AI-driven fight statistics for major events such as Oleksandr Usyk’s victory over Tyson Fury. With teams in Copenhagen, Shenzhen, and Los Angeles, the company now aims to scale its technology to a wider international market.
        
            </p>

The first production batch of 300 systems is already fully pre-ordered and expected to be delivered next year.

Founded in Copenhagen by Allan Svejstrup Nielsen and Elias Obeid, Jabbr has already attracted global attention after delivering AI-driven fight statistics for major events such as Oleksandr Usyk’s victory over Tyson Fury. With teams in Copenhagen, Shenzhen, and Los Angeles, the company now aims to scale its technology to a wider international market." aria-hidden="true" data-delayed-url="https://media.licdn.com/dms/image/v2/D4D22AQEUlOkbioSohQ/feedshare-shrink_800/B4DZnxdZlEJIAg-/0/1760692640555?e=2147483647&amp;v=beta&amp;t=d4aSe69st1IEJvX0WH-iT6iBS8RhMusTJD-Pf38XyeE">

      <img class="inline-block relative

           face-pile__image border-1 border-solid border-color-transparent -ml-2 first:ml-0" data-delayed-url="https://media.licdn.com/dms/image/v2/D4D0BAQGa0mqjWdxm2A/company-logo_100_100/B4DZen9DwrHkAU-/0/1750869491117/tum_think_tank_an_der_hochschule_f_r_politik_m_nchen_logo?e=2147483647&amp;v=beta&amp;t=8xahv2qVOzsypF7wDgJpTH7DZr0Rt9d8s2sZYdP10q0" data-ghost-classes="bg-color-entity-ghost-background" data-ghost-url="https://static.licdn.com/aero-v1/sc/h/9c8pery4andzj6ohjkjp54ma2" alt>

      <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/posts/tum-think-tank-an-der-hochschule-f-r-politik-m-nchen_what-if-the-best-way-to-understand-ai-agents-activity-7405162000751910912-SelR?trk=public_profile_relatedPosts" target="_self" data-tracking-control-name="public_profile_relatedPosts" data-tracking-will-navigate class="base-card relative w-full hover:no-underline focus:no-underline
        base-card--link
        outline-offset-[4px] base-aside-card flex my-1.5
        
        base-aside-card--link
        gap-x-1 mt-0 mb-0.5">
        

<!---->
      
<!---->
        <div class="base-aside-card__info self-center pl-1 flex flex-col flex-1">
          <h3 class="base-aside-card__title font-sans text-md font-bold text-color-text relative">
            
<!---->          </h3>

<!---->
            <p class="base-aside-card__subtitle font-sans text-sm text-color-text leading-regular break-words overflow-anywhere
                line-clamp-2">
              
          What if the best way to understand AI agents is not to study their code, but their behaviour?

In his latest research note, our Fellow of Practice Nicklas Berild Lundblad explores how Tinbergen’s influential ethology framework can help us make sense of increasingly autonomous AI systems. Instead of asking only how models are built, he suggests we also ask how they behave, develop, adapt, and evolve within their environments.

Tracing Tinbergen’s four questions from birdsong to machine behavior, Nicklas shows how the framework offers clear angles of inquiry, including why some agents exhibit overly agreeable behavior even when users are wrong. As modern systems begin to plan, delegate, and act across long time horizons, he suggests it is time to establish a true discipline of agent ethology.

Such a discipline would bring the empirical rigor of behavioral science to AI systems before their patterns become entrenched and their ecologies too complex to untangle.

 Read his full research note here https://lnkd.in/efTe9QKF

cc: Hochschule für Politik München, TUM School of Social Sciences and Technology, Technical University of Munich

        
            </p>

          <h3 class="base-aside-card__title font-sans text-md font-bold text-color-text relative">

<!---->
            <p class="base-aside-card__subtitle font-sans text-sm text-color-text leading-regular break-words overflow-anywhere
                line-clamp-2">
              
          Ny artikel offentliggjort; vi undersøger effekten af TMTM (Tidlig Matematikindsats Til Marginalelever) på kort og lidt længere sigt. Skrevet sammen med Pia Tonnesen, Klaus Rasmussen, Steffen Overgaard, Julie Vangsøe Færch, Signe Gottschau Malm og Jimmy Harder.
Abstract: Running two separate two-stage randomized trials, we implement and test three variants of a small group instruction intervention aimed at improving mathematics competencies for the 20% lowest achievers in mathematics in grades 2 and 8 in Danish public schools. We calculate immediate impacts on math competencies as well as impacts in the medium term and conduct cost-effectiveness analyses of the different intervention arms. The context is the Scandinavian welfare state with an already high-quality public school system. Nevertheless, we find very large positive and cost-effective impacts of several intervention variants, some of which persist in the medium term. In particular, interventions in grade 2 tend to persist, while eighth-grade interventions tend to fade out in the medium term.

https://lnkd.in/didk8En2

      <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/posts/healthau_ai-project-to-transform-cancer-treatment-activity-7344282483493896192-g57T?trk=public_profile_relatedPosts" target="_self" data-tracking-control-name="public_profile_relatedPosts" data-tracking-will-navigate class="base-card relative w-full hover:no-underline focus:no-underline
        base-card--link
        outline-offset-[4px] base-aside-card flex my-1.5
        
        base-aside-card--link
        gap-x-1 mt-0 mb-0.5">
        

<!---->
      
<!---->
        <div class="base-aside-card__info self-center pl-1 flex flex-col flex-1">
          <h3 class="base-aside-card__title font-sans text-md font-bold text-color-text relative">
            
<!---->          </h3>

<!---->
            <p class="base-aside-card__subtitle font-sans text-sm text-color-text leading-regular break-words overflow-anywhere
                line-clamp-2">
              
          AI project to transform cancer treatment receives DKK 53 million in funding

We're proud to announce that Professor Stine Korreman from the Department of Clinical Medicine has been awarded over DKK 53 million from the Novo Nordisk Foundation's Grand AI Challenge for the AIM@CANCER project.

This groundbreaking initiative will use AI and supercomputing to analyze 130 million medical images from Danish radiation therapy clinics – creating the world's largest dataset of its kind. The project involves international collaboration with researchers from Copenhagen, Odense, and New York, with access to the GEFION supercomputer and 15 new research positions.

The aim is to develop an AI model that works like a "large language model for medical images" – one that can optimise and personalise radiation therapy for individual cancer patients whilst making life easier for doctors. 

This will directly help the 14,000 Danish cancer patients who receive radiation therapy each year, and the solutions are designed to make a difference worldwide.

"We're developing an AI model that can make treatment more precise and better suited to the individual patient," says Stine Korreman.

This represents an important step forward in the efforts to use advanced technology for meaningful medical breakthroughs that will improve cancer care.

We look forward to seeing the results of this extraordinary project. 
        
            </p>

           face-pile__image border-1 border-solid border-color-transparent -ml-2 first:ml-0" data-delayed-url="https://media.licdn.com/dms/image/v2/D4D0BAQFYmCxQxlLs5g/company-logo_100_100/company-logo_100_100/0/1704996650867?e=2147483647&amp;v=beta&amp;t=O3Tp6byPQGCrEMeTZeNBg5JC-OSZjFbQG8uQBuckeBY" data-ghost-classes="bg-color-entity-ghost-background" data-ghost-url="https://static.licdn.com/aero-v1/sc/h/9c8pery4andzj6ohjkjp54ma2" alt>

      <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/posts/dtu-mathematics_dataanalysis-statistics-math-activity-7427273623498911744-945X?trk=public_profile_relatedPosts" target="_self" data-tracking-control-name="public_profile_relatedPosts" data-tracking-will-navigate class="base-card relative w-full hover:no-underline focus:no-underline

        <div class="base-aside-card__info self-center pl-1 flex flex-col flex-1">
          <h3 class="base-aside-card__title font-sans text-md font-bold text-color-text relative">
            
<!---->          </h3>

<!---->
            <p class="base-aside-card__subtitle font-sans text-sm text-color-text leading-regular break-words overflow-anywhere
                line-clamp-2">
              
          
𝐃𝐚𝐧𝐢𝐬𝐡 𝐡𝐨𝐦𝐞𝐨𝐰𝐧𝐞𝐫𝐬 have virtually 𝐧𝐨 𝐩𝐨𝐬𝐬𝐢𝐛𝐢𝐥𝐢𝐭𝐲 𝐨𝐟 𝐯𝐞𝐫𝐢𝐟𝐲𝐢𝐧𝐠 the basis for the 𝐜𝐚𝐥𝐜𝐮𝐥𝐚𝐭𝐢𝐨𝐧𝐬 𝐮𝐧𝐝𝐞𝐫𝐥𝐲𝐢𝐧𝐠 their 𝐩𝐫𝐨𝐩𝐞𝐫𝐭𝐲 𝐯𝐚𝐥𝐮𝐚𝐭𝐢𝐨𝐧𝐬 and, consequently, their 𝐡𝐨𝐮𝐬𝐢𝐧𝐠 𝐭𝐚𝐱𝐞𝐬. This is reported by the media house Berlingske, based on investigations carried out by two professors at DTU Compute. 

𝐁𝐨 𝐅𝐫𝐢𝐢𝐬 𝐍𝐢𝐞𝐥𝐬𝐞𝐧 𝐚𝐧𝐝 𝐂𝐚𝐫𝐬𝐭𝐞𝐧 𝐖𝐢𝐭𝐭 have examined a so‑called JSON file to which the Vurderingsstyrelsen (Danish Property Assessment Agency) refers, but which contains such vast amounts of data that it is impossible to gain an overview unless one is a data specialist, and which furthermore links to files that homeowners are unable to open. 

“I do not believe it will be possible in any way to extract the model calculation itself from the JSON file,” says Bo Friis Nielsen, Professor and Head of Section for Statistics and Data Analysis at DTU Compute.

Find the link to the story in the comments. Berlingske has published a number of articles on the property valuations, so do feel free to look for follow‑up stories as well.

#dataanalysis #statistics #math #dkforsk 

DTU - Technical University of Denmark
        
            </p>

          <h3 class="base-aside-card__title font-sans text-md font-bold text-color-text relative">

            <p class="base-aside-card__subtitle font-sans text-sm text-color-text leading-regular break-words overflow-anywhere
                line-clamp-2">
              
          The future isn’t inherited. It’s built.

Today’s startups are tomorrow’s giants. But if we want to lead the next wave of innovation, we need to act now.

Together with founders and leaders from Klarna, Kry, Sana, Amazon, Lovable, EU parliament, EQT, Accel, Nasdaq and more, we just published an open letter in Dagens Industri with one message:

The Nordics can lead. But not without serious change.

We call out three moves that cannot wait:

Cut the red tape - Innovation dies in complexity. Europe has the scale. Now we need speed. Let founders build instead of filling out forms.

Back the talent - Great companies are built by great people. We need to equip students, workers and researchers with real tools like AI and quantum. And build a culture where learning never stops.

Unleash capital and technology - We have built global companies before. We can do it again. But only if we make Norden the best place to start and scale. That means easier access to capital, to deep tech, and to partnerships across sectors.

The next platform shift is already happening. The question is whether we build the future here, or watch it happen somewhere else.

We choose to build. Because the future isn’t inherited. It’s built.

Written and signed by me and:

Johannes Schildt, Sebastian Siemiatkowski, Anton Osika, Joel Hellermark, Arba Kokalari, Kitty Mayo, Gulfem Toygar, Matt Robinson, Johan Brenner, Daniel Waterhouse, Elis Hodzic, Sandra Malmberg 👋, Adam Kostyal and Ludvig Bartholdsson

Full article (in Swedish + English translation) in comments.
        
            </p>

      <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/posts/ken-pfeuffer-404377129_xr-visionpro-lightingdesign-activity-7345928597343277056-ojj-?trk=public_profile_relatedPosts" target="_self" data-tracking-control-name="public_profile_relatedPosts" data-tracking-will-navigate class="base-card relative w-full hover:no-underline focus:no-underline

        <div class="base-aside-card__info self-center pl-1 flex flex-col flex-1">
          <h3 class="base-aside-card__title font-sans text-md font-bold text-color-text relative">
            
<!---->          </h3>

<!---->
            <p class="base-aside-card__subtitle font-sans text-sm text-color-text leading-regular break-words overflow-anywhere
                line-clamp-2">
              
          XR Light Designer with Apple Vision Pro

Really proud to share an extraordinary Master’s thesis project by Mads Kristian Steen Vejrup, Oliver Due Nielsen, and Magnus Frisk from Department of Computer Science, Aarhus University, supported by Pioneer Centre for AI (P1).

🎓 Title: XR Light Designer: A Standalone Application for Lighting Design and Pre-Visualization on the Apple Vision Pro (2025)

This thesis explores how XR, especially Apple Vision Pro, can shift lighting design from a technical, screen-based task into something more spatial, intuitive, and collaborative.

🎯 Use cases explored:

🎬 Pre-Visualization Tool (00:35) – Prototype and test lighting designs in immersive versions of real venues
🎤 Externalization Tool (01:16) – Let directors, performers, etc., express lighting ideas without technical skills
🤝 Conversation Tool (03:13) – Help experts and non-experts collaborate on lighting setups (in person or remote)
🎭 Mixed Reality (04:26) - Mixing physical and virtual fixtures

User research &amp; findings
The project included participatory design and user studies with both domain experts and non-experts:

✔️ A non-technical artist appreciated the ability to spatially prototype lighting instead of relying on 2D tools
✔️ A lighting technician saw less value in design features but emphasized the collaborative potential
✔️ Lay users could use the system without prior training—highlighting how accessible and intuitive it is, even for newcomers

This project points toward a future where immersive lighting design is not only professional-grade and spatially grounded, but also collaborative and inclusive. ✨ 

If you're curious and want to check out the full report, feel free to reach out to any of us! 

Kudos to Mads, Oliver and Magnus, extremely talented and creative students who have came up with the concept and implementations by themselves.

Supervisors: 🧢 Tobias Langlotz &amp; me.

Notably, this project builds up on an early exploration that we shared end of last year. 

#XR  Apple #VisionPro #LightingDesign #AR #VR #Unity3D #DMX #AarhusUniversity #gaze #pinch
        
            </p>

    <div class="aside-activity-card ">
      
      
    

    
      <a href="https://dk.linkedin.com/in/carsten-baum?trk=public_profile_relatedPosts_face-pile-cta" target="_self" data-tracking-control-name="full-link" data-tracking-will-navigate class="face-pile flex !no-underline">
        
      <div class="face-pile__images-container self-start flex-shrink-0 mr-1 leading-[1]">
          
      <img class="inline-block relative
          rounded-[50%]
          w-4 h-4
           face-pile__image border-1 border-solid border-color-transparent -ml-2 first:ml-0" data-delayed-url="https://media.licdn.com/dms/image/v2/D4E03AQGn39QU5y_fCQ/profile-displayphoto-shrink_200_200/profile-displayphoto-shrink_200_200/0/1678779726876?e=2147483647&amp;v=beta&amp;t=MTQbSZo_sBlF4UjEd4RCgt_hSRDxs_osRRZ2uSlrwW4" data-ghost-classes="bg-color-entity-ghost-background" data-ghost-url="https://static.licdn.com/aero-v1/sc/h/9c8pery4andzj6ohjkjp54ma2" alt>

            <p class="face-pile__metadata font-sans text-xs leading-open text-color-text-low-emphasis -mt-0.5">DTU Compute
                 • 2K followers</p>

      <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/posts/carsten-baum_faster-proofs-and-vrfs-from-isogenies-activity-7361285544934367232-eAhl?trk=public_profile_relatedPosts" target="_self" data-tracking-control-name="public_profile_relatedPosts" data-tracking-will-navigate class="base-card relative w-full hover:no-underline focus:no-underline
        base-card--link
        outline-offset-[4px] base-aside-card flex my-1.5
        
        base-aside-card--link
        gap-x-1 mt-0 mb-0.5">
        

<!---->
      
<!---->
        <div class="base-aside-card__info self-center pl-1 flex flex-col flex-1">
          <h3 class="base-aside-card__title font-sans text-md font-bold text-color-text relative">
            
<!---->          </h3>

<!---->
            <p class="base-aside-card__subtitle font-sans text-sm text-color-text leading-regular break-words overflow-anywhere
                line-clamp-2">
              
          The traditional Danish summer vacation (which the rest of the world just calls ``July'') ended recently, and DTU Compute Cryptography group is kicking off the new academic year with 3 accepted papers at IACR ASIACRYPT 2025!

Christian Majenz, together with Andreas Hülsing and Mikhail Kudinov from Eindhoven University, got a paper accepted that improved the security analysis of a hash function property called multi-target extended target collision resistance. Their work furthers our understanding of the security of the recently standardized Falcon signature scheme (and allows to choose more efficient parameters for it!) as well as of signature aggregation schemes. The paper is already on eprint: https://lnkd.in/dJSx2hH5.

Luisa Siniscalchi, together with Divya Ravi from the University of Amsterdam and Michele Ciampi and Yu Xia from the University of Edinburgh, show how to build, making black box use of the underlying cryptography, optimal-round dishonest-majority MPC protocols when the broadcast channel is available only in certain rounds. This greatly improves over the state-of-the-art, as black box use of cryptography is usually preferrable in terms of efficiency and practicality.

Finally, my postdoc Robi Pedersen, together with Shai Levin from the University of Auckland, improved recent results on zero-knowledge proofs of isogeny knowledge by encoding these in an optimized fashion as an R1CS statement. This allows them to use generic (and highly optimized) SNARK proof systems as a backend, speeding up previous approaches. In addition, they show how this leads to a new isogeny-based VRF construction. The paper is on eprint: https://lnkd.in/dkNkHBbV.

        
            </p>

          <img alt="The traditional Danish summer vacation (which the rest of the world just calls ``July'') ended recently, and DTU Compute Cryptography group is kicking off the new academic year with 3 accepted papers at IACR ASIACRYPT 2025!

Christian Majenz, together with Andreas Hülsing and Mikhail Kudinov from Eindhoven University, got a paper accepted that improved the security analysis of a hash function property called multi-target extended target collision resistance. Their work furthers our understanding of the security of the recently standardized Falcon signature scheme (and allows to choose more efficient parameters for it!) as well as of signature aggregation schemes. The paper is already on eprint: https://lnkd.in/dJSx2hH5.

Luisa Siniscalchi, together with Divya Ravi from the University of Amsterdam and Michele Ciampi and Yu Xia from the University of Edinburgh, show how to build, making black box use of the underlying cryptography, optimal-round dishonest-majority MPC protocols when the broadcast channel is available only in certain rounds. This greatly improves over the state-of-the-art, as black box use of cryptography is usually preferrable in terms of efficiency and practicality.

Finally, my postdoc Robi Pedersen, together with Shai Levin from the University of Auckland, improved recent results on zero-knowledge proofs of isogeny knowledge by encoding these in an optimized fashion as an R1CS statement. This allows them to use generic (and highly optimized) SNARK proof systems as a backend, speeding up previous approaches. In addition, they show how this leads to a new isogeny-based VRF construction. The paper is on eprint: https://lnkd.in/dkNkHBbV.

            <p class="base-aside-card__subtitle font-sans text-sm text-color-text leading-regular break-words overflow-anywhere
                line-clamp-2">
              
          💡 Innovation in the classroom!
James Wen, professor in Human-Computer Interaction at Molde University College — and originally from New York — found it challenging to read Norwegian students’ poker faces during lectures.

His solution? He made Enhancing Lecture Flow (ELF) — a new app designed to make feedback between students and teachers simpler and more effective.

ELF has already received positive feedback from students who participated in the pilot project.

“An innovative idea like this has been long-awaited for my part. I don’t understand why it hasn’t been a thing earlier,” says student Anna Kristín Indriðadóttir.

At Molde University College, we believe in pushing the boundaries of how we engage students — and ELF is an excellent example of that. We’re particularly interested in how tools like this can support active learning, real-time feedback, and better student outcomes.

We’d love to hear from colleagues: how are you using digital tools to boost student engagement?

🔗 Read the full article from Norsk rikskringkasting (NRK) (in Norwegian):

https://lnkd.in/dAG67dUu

 #EdTech #AcademicInnovation #StudentEngagement #HiMolde

      <a href="https://dk.linkedin.com/in/christian-lohmann-dixa?trk=public_profile_relatedPosts_face-pile-cta" target="_self" data-tracking-control-name="full-link" data-tracking-will-navigate class="face-pile flex !no-underline">
        
      <div class="face-pile__images-container self-start flex-shrink-0 mr-1 leading-[1]">
          
      <img class="inline-block relative
          rounded-[50%]
          w-4 h-4
          bg-color-entity-ghost-background face-pile__image border-1 border-solid border-color-transparent -ml-2 first:ml-0" data-delayed-url="https://static.licdn.com/aero-v1/sc/h/9c8pery4andzj6ohjkjp54ma2" data-ghost-classes="bg-color-entity-ghost-background" data-ghost-url="https://static.licdn.com/aero-v1/sc/h/9c8pery4andzj6ohjkjp54ma2" alt>

        <div class="face-pile__text-container self-center">
          <p class="face-pile__text font-sans text-sm
              link-styled hover:underline">
            Christian Lohmann

            <p class="face-pile__metadata font-sans text-xs leading-open text-color-text-low-emphasis -mt-0.5">Dixa

      </a>
  
  
    
    
      <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/posts/christian-lohmann-dixa_i-judged-an-ai-hackathon-zero2demo-for-dtu-activity-7401591095450812417-_Kkm?trk=public_profile_relatedPosts" target="_self" data-tracking-control-name="public_profile_relatedPosts" data-tracking-will-navigate class="base-card relative w-full hover:no-underline focus:no-underline
        base-card--link
        outline-offset-[4px] base-aside-card flex my-1.5
        
        base-aside-card--link
        gap-x-1 mt-0 mb-0.5">
        

<!---->
      
<!---->
        <div class="base-aside-card__info self-center pl-1 flex flex-col flex-1">
          <h3 class="base-aside-card__title font-sans text-md font-bold text-color-text relative">
            
<!---->          </h3>

<!---->
            <p class="base-aside-card__subtitle font-sans text-sm text-color-text leading-regular break-words overflow-anywhere
                line-clamp-2">
              
          I judged an AI Hackathon Zero2Demo for DTU x CBS students over the weekend - and it completely flipped one of my “AI-Assumptions”. I used to think AI would mostly replace junior roles. Now I’m not so sure anymore. 

Students using AI today can reach “expert-level” execution absurdly fast. They build things in hours that used to take teams months.

And sure – not everything can be solved by predicting the next token in a model. Some experience comes from years of scars, bad decisions, and awkward meetings you wish you could undo. But let’s be honest… a surprising amount of “experience” is really just pattern recognition. And AI is very good at patterns. (Sometimes too good… it spots patterns that don’t even exist.)

So who’s at risk? Not juniors, not seniors either. It’s anyone, at any level, who stops adapting.

AI won’t reward seniority nor experience. It will reward curiosity and speed of learning - which is great news for students.  

Massive shoutout to the partners who made this possible: Antler, byFounders, node.vc , People Ventures, Creator Fund, Wave Ventures, United Founders, Lovable, Cursor, TechBBQ, and all other incredible sponsors. Huge kudos to the organizers Matyas Adam Michel, Milan Aha, Adam Bočev, and Janik Pöttinger!
        
            </p>

<!---->
            <div class="base-aside-card__metadata font-sans text-sm leading-open font-regular text-color-text-low-emphasis">
              
          
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    
    

    <code id="i18n_reaction_singular" style="display: none"><!--"%numReactions% Reaction"--></code>

          <img alt="I judged an AI Hackathon Zero2Demo for DTU x CBS students over the weekend - and it completely flipped one of my “AI-Assumptions”. I used to think AI would mostly replace junior roles. Now I’m not so sure anymore. 

Students using AI today can reach “expert-level” execution absurdly fast. They build things in hours that used to take teams months.

And sure – not everything can be solved by predicting the next token in a model. Some experience comes from years of scars, bad decisions, and awkward meetings you wish you could undo. But let’s be honest… a surprising amount of “experience” is really just pattern recognition. And AI is very good at patterns. (Sometimes too good… it spots patterns that don’t even exist.)

So who’s at risk? Not juniors, not seniors either. It’s anyone, at any level, who stops adapting.

AI won’t reward seniority nor experience. It will reward curiosity and speed of learning - which is great news for students.  

Massive shoutout to the partners who made this possible: Antler, byFounders, node.vc , People Ventures, Creator Fund, Wave Ventures, United Founders, Lovable, Cursor, TechBBQ, and all other incredible sponsors. Huge kudos to the organizers Matyas Adam Michel, Milan Aha, Adam Bočev, and Janik Pöttinger!" aria-hidden="true" data-delayed-url="https://media.licdn.com/dms/image/v2/D4D22AQHpAkYaqd7tSw/feedshare-shrink_1280/B4DZrevNnXG0Ak-/0/1764673510619?e=2147483647&amp;v=beta&amp;t=sfUq-fCulrWgfrro1_95S-Qs3A0h-B13gBBGe9WxL7I">
